Canonical inbox + dispatch workerSingle source of truth; easy to retry/replayPer-channel collections — consistency nightmare
Change streams for fan-outPush-based, low latency, durablePolling — misses, lag, load
Per-category preferencesUser-level granular mutingGlobal on/off — users disable everything
Quiet hours snoozingRespects user time zoneSend always — complaints, opt-outs
Push tokens in preferencesCo-located with delivery rulesSeparate devices collection — extra read

Production polish: use specialized notification platforms — Knock, Courier, Customer.io, Braze, or OneSignal — that handle channel orchestration, batching, throttling, and delivery analytics, so you don’t reinvent retries and bounce handling; push delivery via APNs (iOS), FCM (Android), Web Push API; email via Postmark/Resend/SendGrid with React Email/MJML templates; SMS via Twilio/MessageBird; in-app real-time via WebSockets (Pusher/Ably/Liveblocks); batching — group multiple mentions into a digest after 5 min of inactivity; frequency capping — max 3 marketing pushes per day; delivery tracking via webhook callbacks updating notification status; preferences UI mounted at /settings/notifications with granular toggles; soft-bounce/unsubscribe handling auto-disables channels; compliance: GDPR/CCPA opt-out tracked in preferences, audit log of marketing sends.

Question 56

Explain how you would implement a search engine optimization (SEO) strategy for a MongoDB-backed website.

Situation: a MongoDB-backed website needs strong SEO — fast page loads, server-rendered HTML, structured data, clean URLs, sitemaps, canonical URLs, fresh content, and no duplicate content issues. Google’s ranking depends on technical SEO; the database schema must support it.

Approach: denormalize SEO fields directly into content documents (slug, title, meta_description, og_image), pre-render HTML at publish time (don’t parse Markdown on every request), maintain a sitemap_entries view via $merge, and use canonical URL fields to handle duplicates. The application layer (Next.js, Astro, Remix) does SSR/SSG against MongoDB.

// articles — SEO fields denormalized
db.articles.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  slug: "understanding-mongodb-indexes",
  canonical_url: "https://example.com/blog/understanding-mongodb-indexes",
  status: "published",
  seo: {
    title: "Understanding MongoDB Indexes – Example Blog",
    description: "A 2026 guide to compound indexes, ESR, and Atlas Performance Advisor.",
    keywords: ["mongodb", "indexes", "performance"],
    og_image: "https://cdn.example.com/og/mongodb-indexes.png",
    twitter_card: "summary_large_image"
  },
  content_html: "...",   // pre-rendered, fast to serve
  published_at: new Date(),
  updated_at: new Date(),
  word_count: 1842,
  schema_org: {
    "@type": "BlogPosting",
    "headline": "Understanding MongoDB Indexes",
    "datePublished": "2026-04-29T10:00:00Z",
    "author": { "@type": "Person", "name": "Alice Cole" }
  }
})

// Indexes for SEO routes
db.articles.createIndex({ slug: 1 }, { unique: true })
db.articles.createIndex({ status: 1, published_at: -1 })   // archive pages
db.articles.createIndex({ "seo.keywords": 1 })

// Sitemap generation — materialized via $merge nightly
db.articles.aggregate([
  { $match: { status: "published" } },
  { $project: {
      _id: 0,
      url:        { $concat: ["https://example.com/blog/", "$slug"] },
      lastmod:    "$updated_at",
      changefreq: "weekly",
      priority:   0.7
  }},
  { $merge: "sitemap_entries" }
])

// Canonical URLs for syndicated content
db.articles.updateOne(
  { _id: syndicatedId },
  { $set: { canonical_url: "https://original-site.com/post-slug" } }
)

// 301 redirects for renamed slugs
db.redirects.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  from_path: "/blog/old-slug",
  to_path:   "/blog/new-slug",
  status_code: 301,
  created_at: new Date()
})
db.redirects.createIndex({ from_path: 1 }, { unique: true })

Trade-offs:

DecisionWhyAlternative
Pre-rendered HTMLFast TTFB; no Markdown parsing per requestRender-on-read — CPU per request, slower
SEO fields on the documentSingle-doc fetch renders the full <head>Compute at request — redundant work
Materialized sitemapGeneration is offline; serving is O(1) readLive aggregate — minutes to compute on large blogs
Canonical URL fieldHandles syndication; dedup signals to GoogleNone — duplicate content penalty
Redirects collection301 rewrites preserve link equity on slug changesHard-coded in app — redeploy for every change

Production polish: SSR/SSG via Next.js/Astro/Remix/SvelteKit — static export to Vercel/Cloudflare Pages/Netlify for instant TTFB; ISR (incremental static regeneration) revalidates pages on publish via webhooks from change streams; image optimization via Cloudinary/imgix/Vercel Image Optimization/next/image; structured data validation via Schema.org JSON-LD; Core Web Vitals monitored via Vercel Speed Insights/Cloudflare Web Analytics/WebPageTest; internal linking — related articles via Atlas Vector Search on embeddings; duplicate detection across the site via canonical URLs and noindex on faceted navigation; RSS/Atom feeds generated from the same query as the sitemap; robots.txt, llms.txt served from the edge; analytics via Plausible/Fathom/PostHog (privacy-preserving); for international SEO, hreflang tags driven by per-locale article documents; SEO audits via Ahrefs/Semrush/Screaming Frog.

Question 57

You are asked to design a schema for a crowdfunding platform with campaigns, backers, and pledges. How would you structure the collections?

Situation: a crowdfunding platform with campaigns, backers, pledges, and rewards. Campaigns have funding goals and deadlines; pledges may be conditional (only charged if goal met); reward tiers ship physical or digital goods. Reads dominate (campaign pages); pledge writes spike around launches and deadlines.

Approach: four collections. campaigns holds the canonical campaign with embedded reward tiers; pledges is the ledger of every commitment (pending, charged, refunded); backers is a denormalized roll-up per user per campaign; updates hold creator posts. Funding totals are denormalized for fast reads with a periodic reconcile.

// campaigns — with embedded reward tiers
db.campaigns.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  creator_id: ObjectId("..."),
  title: "Open-Source Coffee Grinder",
  slug: "opensource-grinder",
  category: "design",
  goal_cents: 5_000_000,                  // $50,000
  raised_cents: 0,                         // denormalized
  backer_count: 0,                          // denormalized
  status: "live",                           // draft | live | succeeded | failed | cancelled
  starts_at:    ISODate("2026-04-01"),
  ends_at:      ISODate("2026-05-31"),
  rewards: [
    { _id: "tier_early_bird", title: "Early Bird", price_cents: 19900,
      description: "Get the grinder — saves $50", limit: 100, claimed: 0,
      ships: { regions: ["US", "EU"], estimate: ISODate("2026-12-01") } },
    { _id: "tier_standard",   title: "Standard",   price_cents: 24900,
      description: "Get the grinder", limit: null, claimed: 0,
      ships: { regions: ["US", "EU"], estimate: ISODate("2027-01-15") } }
  ],
  story_html: "..."
})

// pledges — the ledger
db.pledges.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  campaign_id: ObjectId("..."),
  backer_id:   ObjectId("..."),
  reward_id:   "tier_early_bird",
  amount_cents: 19900,
  status: "pending",                       // pending | charged | refunded | failed
  payment: { provider: "stripe", intent_id: "pi_..." },
  shipping: { name: "Alice Smith", address: { /* ... */ } },
  pledged_at: new Date()
})

// Place a pledge atomically (with limit enforcement)
const session = client.startSession()
await session.withTransaction(async () => {
  const result = await db.campaigns.updateOne(
    { _id: campaign_id, "rewards._id": "tier_early_bird",
      $expr: { $lt: [
        { $arrayElemAt: ["$rewards.claimed", { $indexOfArray: ["$rewards._id", "tier_early_bird"] }] },
        { $arrayElemAt: ["$rewards.limit",   { $indexOfArray: ["$rewards._id", "tier_early_bird"] }] }
      ]}
    },
    { $inc: { "rewards.$.claimed": 1, raised_cents: 19900, backer_count: 1 } },
    { session }
  )
  if (result.modifiedCount === 0) throw new Error("reward_sold_out")
  await db.pledges.insertOne({ /* pledge */ }, { session })
})

// On campaign deadline: succeed or refund
db.campaigns.updateOne({ _id, ends_at: { $lt: new Date() }, status: "live",
  $expr: { $gte: ["$raised_cents", "$goal_cents"] } },
  { $set: { status: "succeeded" } })

// Indexes
db.campaigns.createIndex({ status: 1, ends_at: 1 })
db.campaigns.createIndex({ creator_id: 1 })
db.pledges.createIndex({ campaign_id: 1, pledged_at: -1 })
db.pledges.createIndex({ backer_id: 1, pledged_at: -1 })

Trade-offs:

DecisionWhyAlternative
Embed rewards in campaignOne read renders campaign pageSeparate rewards — $lookup per render
Denormalized totalsCampaign page loads in O(1)Live $sum — thousands of pledges scanned
Conditional update with $exprAtomic limit enforcement; no oversellRead-then-check — race conditions
All-or-nothing model (Kickstarter)Pledges captured at deadline only if goal metCharge immediately — refund mass on failure
Pending → charged status flowReflects payment lifecycleSingle status — can’t represent “intent vs settled”

Production polish: payments via Stripe (Issue PaymentIntent with capture_method: "manual" for delayed capture at deadline); fraud scoring via Stripe Radar/Sift; shipping address validation via EasyPost/Shippo/Lob; fulfillment integrations to ShipStation/Pirate Ship; creator dashboards via Atlas Charts or custom React; change streams trigger fundraising milestone notifications via Knock/Customer.io; email/SMS updates to backers via Postmark+Twilio; reconciliation: nightly job recomputes raised_cents from pledges, alerts on drift; tax compliance via Stripe Tax/Avalara/TaxJar; currency: store all amounts in cents (Decimal128 for multi-currency); analytics exported to BigQuery/Snowflake; community features (comments, updates) tied to the campaign; creator KYC via Persona/Onfido/Stripe Identity; archived campaigns kept indefinitely for trust signals; ToS enforcement via reports queue moderated through Hive/Sift.

Question 58

How would you handle multi-language support and localization in MongoDB?

Situation: the application supports multiple languages (English, Spanish, French, Japanese...) for UI strings, content (articles, products), and user-generated text. Translations are partial — English may be ahead of Japanese; users prefer their locale and fall back to defaults; SEO needs language-specific URLs.

Approach: two patterns based on data type. UI strings live in a translations file/service (i18next, FormatJS), not MongoDB. Content with locale variants uses locale-keyed subdocs on the same parent — { title: { en: "...", es: "...", fr: "..." } } — so one fetch returns all variants and fallback is in-memory.

// products — locale-keyed fields
db.products.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  sku: "WIDGET-001",
  price_cents: 2999,
  // Per-locale content
  name: {
    en: "Premium Widget",
    es: "Widget Premium",
    fr: "Widget Haut de Gamme",
    ja: "プレミアムウィジェット"
  },
  description: {
    en: "A high-quality widget...",
    es: "Un widget de alta calidad...",
    fr: "Un widget de haute qualité..."
    // ja missing — will fall back to en
  },
  default_locale: "en",
  available_locales: ["en", "es", "fr", "ja"],
  created_at: new Date()
})

// Application reads with fallback
function localized(field, locale, fallback = "en") {
  return field[locale] ?? field[fallback]
}
const product = await db.products.findOne({ sku: "WIDGET-001" })
const name = localized(product.name, userLocale)

// Aggregation: project the right locale server-side
db.products.aggregate([
  { $project: {
      sku: 1, price_cents: 1,
      name: { $ifNull: [`$name.${userLocale}`, "$name.en"] },
      description: { $ifNull: [`$description.${userLocale}`, "$description.en"] }
  }}
])

// Slugs per locale for SEO
db.articles.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  slugs: {
    en: "how-to-bake-bread",
    es: "como-hornear-pan",
    fr: "comment-cuire-le-pain"
  },
  hreflang: ["en", "es", "fr"],   // for <link rel="alternate" hreflang> tags
  // ...
})
db.articles.createIndex({ "slugs.en": 1 }, { unique: true, sparse: true })
db.articles.createIndex({ "slugs.es": 1 }, { unique: true, sparse: true })
db.articles.createIndex({ "slugs.fr": 1 }, { unique: true, sparse: true })

// User preference
db.users.updateOne({ _id: userId }, { $set: { locale: "es", currency: "EUR" } })

// Translation collection (for translator workflow)
db.translation_jobs.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  source: { type: "product", id: ObjectId("..."), field: "description", locale: "en" },
  target_locale: "ja",
  status: "pending",            // pending | in_progress | review | published
  assignee: ObjectId("..."),
  due_at: ISODate("...")
})

Trade-offs:

DecisionWhyAlternative
Locale-keyed subdocsOne read, no joins; clean fallback logicPer-locale collection — multi-collection consistency
UI strings outside DBStatic, deployable, versioned with codeDB strings — cache invalidation pain, no compile-time checks
App-side fallback chainFlexible (en → en-US → en-GB)DB-side $ifNull — less flexible, slower
Slugs per localeSEO-friendly URLs in each languageSingle English slug — bad UX, lost local search rank
Sparse unique indexes per locale slugEach slug unique within its localeComposite slug+locale — hard to enforce

Production polish: use i18next/FormatJS/next-intl for UI string management with ICU MessageFormat for plurals and dates; translation management systems — Lokalise, Crowdin, Transifex, Phrase, or POEditor — for translator workflows with versioning and review; machine translation via DeepL/Google Translate API/OpenAI GPT-4 for first drafts; locale detection via Accept-Language header with user override; currency formatting via Intl.NumberFormat; date formatting via Intl.DateTimeFormat with date-fns-tz/luxon for time zones; SEO: <link rel="alternate" hreflang> tags for every translated variant, separate sitemaps per locale, region-specific subdomains/paths (/en/, /es/); RTL support (Arabic, Hebrew) requires CSS logical properties; quality monitoring — flag products where translation lags > 7 days; Atlas Search with locale-specific analyzers for proper tokenization (Japanese kuromoji, Chinese Smart Chinese).

Question 59

Describe how you would implement a schema for a food delivery platform with restaurants, menus, and orders.

Situation: a food delivery platform with restaurants, menus, and orders. Restaurants update menus and prices throughout the day; orders are time-sensitive (kitchen prep, courier dispatch); availability depends on restaurant open hours and current order load. Search ranks results by location, cuisine, and ETA.

Approach: four collections. restaurants holds canonical restaurant data with location and hours; menus nests menu sections and items (versioned snapshots so old orders survive menu changes); orders snapshot the items at checkout; a denormalized restaurant_status updates frequently to reflect current load and prep time. Geospatial index on restaurant location.

// restaurants
db.restaurants.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  name: "Joe’s Pizza",
  cuisines: ["italian", "pizza"],
  rating: 4.5,
  price_level: 2,                  // 1 = $, 2 = $$, 3 = $$$
  location: { type: "Point", coordinates: [-73.9857, 40.7484] },
  address: { line1: "...", city: "NYC", zip: "10003" },
  hours: {
    mon: [{ open: "11:00", close: "23:00" }],
    tue: [{ open: "11:00", close: "23:00" }]
    // ...
  },
  delivery: { radius_km: 5, min_order_cents: 1000, fee_cents: 299 },
  active: true
})

// menus — versioned, current pointer
db.menus.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  restaurant_id: ObjectId("..."),
  version: 12,
  current: true,
  sections: [
    { name: "Pizza", items: [
      { _id: "pep_lg", name: "Pepperoni Pizza", price_cents: 1899,
        description: "Classic pepperoni", image: "...",
        options: [
          { name: "Size", choices: [
            { name: "Small", price_delta_cents: 0 },
            { name: "Large", price_delta_cents: 400 }
          ]}
        ],
        available: true
      }
    ]}
  ],
  effective_at: new Date()
})

// orders — snapshot items
db.orders.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  user_id: ObjectId("..."),
  restaurant_id: ObjectId("..."),
  status: "placed",   // placed | accepted | preparing | out_for_delivery | delivered | cancelled
  items: [
    { item_id: "pep_lg", name: "Pepperoni Pizza", price_cents: 1899,
      options: [{ name: "Size", choice: "Large", price_delta_cents: 400 }],
      quantity: 1, line_total_cents: 2299 }
  ],
  totals: { subtotal_cents: 2299, delivery_fee_cents: 299, tax_cents: 207,
            tip_cents: 400, total_cents: 3205 },
  delivery_address: { line1: "...", coords: [-73.99, 40.75] },
  estimates: { prep_minutes: 15, delivery_minutes: 25, ready_at: ISODate("...") },
  placed_at: new Date()
})

// restaurant_status — high-write, denormalized current state
db.restaurant_status.updateOne(
  { _id: restaurantId },
  { $set: {
      open: true,
      orders_in_kitchen: 8,
      avg_prep_minutes: 18,
      accepting_orders: true,
      updated_at: new Date()
  }}, { upsert: true }
)

// Search "pizza near me, open now, ETA < 30 min"
db.restaurants.aggregate([
  { $geoNear: {
      near: { type: "Point", coordinates: [userLng, userLat] },
      distanceField: "distance_meters",
      maxDistance: 5000,
      spherical: true,
      query: { cuisines: "pizza", active: true }
  }},
  { $lookup: {
      from: "restaurant_status",
      localField: "_id", foreignField: "_id",
      as: "status"
  }},
  { $match: { "status.0.accepting_orders": true } },
  { $limit: 50 }
])

// Indexes
db.restaurants.createIndex({ location: "2dsphere" })
db.restaurants.createIndex({ cuisines: 1, rating: -1 })
db.menus.createIndex({ restaurant_id: 1, current: 1 })
db.orders.createIndex({ restaurant_id: 1, status: 1, placed_at: -1 })
db.orders.createIndex({ user_id: 1, placed_at: -1 })

Trade-offs:

DecisionWhyAlternative
Versioned menus + current pointerOld orders survive menu changes; rollback is easySingle mutable menu — rewrites history
Snapshot order itemsReceipts accurate even when prices changeReference menu — broken when item retired
Separate restaurant_statusHot updates don’t churn the restaurant docSingle doc — write contention, cache thrashing
2dsphere on restaurantSub-ms “near me” queriesCity filter only — misses nearby zones
Embedded options/sections in menuOne read renders the menu pageSeparate options collection — multiple round trips

Production polish: live courier tracking via WebSockets (Pusher/Ably) + change streams; routing/ETA via Google Maps Distance Matrix/Mapbox Directions; payments via Stripe/Adyen; fraud detection via Sift/Stripe Radar; tipping integrated; reviews and ratings as a separate collection joined via $lookup for restaurant pages; menu images via Cloudinary/imgix; push notifications at every status change via OneSignal/Firebase/Twilio SMS; order assignment to couriers via a queue (BullMQ/Inngest) with auction-style routing; kitchen display systems integrate via WebSocket subscriptions to restaurant order streams; analytics: hourly demand forecasting via BigQuery/Snowflake → ML models in Vertex AI/SageMaker; surge pricing when demand spikes; compliance: food handling cert tracking, tax (Stripe Tax/Avalara), allergen labels per item, accessibility (alt text on images); partner onboarding via Stripe Connect for direct payouts to restaurants.

Question 60

You need to design a database for a fitness tracking app with users, workouts, and goals. How would you structure the collections?

Situation: a fitness tracking app with users, workouts (cardio, strength, yoga), and goals (steps/day, weight loss, run a 5K). Users log workouts manually or auto-import from Apple Health, Google Fit, Strava, Garmin. Goals track progress over time; charts show trends.

Approach: three collections. users hold profile and current goals; workouts are time-series-style with rich type-specific subdocs; goal_progress is a daily roll-up materialized via aggregation for fast dashboards. Real-time imports go through change streams to keep dashboards fresh.

// users
db.users.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  email: "alice@example.com",
  profile: { display_name: "Alice", height_cm: 168, weight_kg: 65, dob: ISODate("1990-05-12") },
  goals: [
    { _id: "goal_daily_steps", type: "daily_steps", target: 10_000, active: true,
      started_at: new Date() },
    { _id: "goal_weight",      type: "weight",      target_kg: 60,    active: true,
      started_at: new Date() }
  ],
  connected_apps: [
    { provider: "apple_health", connected_at: new Date(), last_sync: new Date() }
  ]
})

// workouts — time-series collection
db.createCollection("workouts", {
  timeseries: { timeField: "started_at", metaField: "meta", granularity: "minutes" }
})
db.workouts.insertOne({
  started_at: ISODate("2026-04-29T07:00:00Z"),
  meta: { user_id: ObjectId("..."), type: "run" },
  source: "strava",
  duration_seconds: 1842,
  distance_meters: 5012,
  calories: 312,
  details: {
    type: "run",
    pace_seconds_per_km: 367,
    avg_hr: 152,
    max_hr: 178,
    elevation_gain_m: 28,
    splits: [/* per-km */ ]
  }
})

// daily_summaries — materialized via $merge nightly
db.workouts.aggregate([
  { $match: { started_at: { $gte: yesterday, $lt: today } } },
  { $group: {
      _id: {
        user_id: "$meta.user_id",
        date: { $dateTrunc: { date: "$started_at", unit: "day" } }
      },
      total_calories:    { $sum: "$calories" },
      total_distance_m:  { $sum: "$distance_meters" },
      total_duration_s:  { $sum: "$duration_seconds" },
      workout_count:     { $sum: 1 }
  }},
  { $merge: {
      into: "daily_summaries",
      on: "_id",
      whenMatched: "replace",
      whenNotMatched: "insert"
  }}
])

// Goal progress query — today’s steps vs target
const today = await db.daily_summaries.findOne({
  "_id.user_id": userId,
  "_id.date": { $eq: startOfToday }
})

// Indexes
db.workouts.createIndex({ "meta.user_id": 1, started_at: -1 })
db.workouts.createIndex({ "meta.user_id": 1, "meta.type": 1, started_at: -1 })
db.daily_summaries.createIndex({ "_id.user_id": 1, "_id.date": -1 })

Trade-offs:

DecisionWhyAlternative
Time-series collection10x compression on dense workout dataRegular collection — storage 10x larger
Materialized daily summariesDashboard reads in O(1) per dayLive aggregation per page load — slow
Type-specific details subdocStrength sets, run splits, yoga poses each have shapePolymorphic columns — inconsistent
Embedded goals on userOne read renders dashboard with goals + progressSeparate collection — extra round trip
Source field on workoutProvenance (manual/strava/garmin); de-dupe by sourceNone — double-import bugs

Production polish: integrations via Strava API, Apple HealthKit, Google Fit / Health Connect, Garmin Connect IQ, Whoop, Oura, Fitbit Web API — OAuth + webhook subscriptions for real-time sync; de-duplication across sources via (provider, external_id) unique index; charts via Atlas Charts/Recharts/Chart.js/D3; route maps rendered with Mapbox/MapTiler from GPS streams; activity recognition (auto-detect run vs bike) via on-device ML or OpenAI Whisper-style audio cues; workout library with prescribed plans (couch-to-5K) via Hevy/Strong-style structured workouts; social features (kudos, segments) need separate collections with denormalized counts; push notifications for goal progress milestones via OneSignal/Firebase; calorie estimation via MET tables or per-user models; health data privacy — HIPAA-aware encryption (Queryable Encryption 7.0+) for sensitive metrics; insights via weekly digest emails generated from rollups; export raw data as JSON/GPX for user portability (GDPR/HIPAA right to access).

Question 61

How would you implement a logging system that captures and stores application logs in MongoDB?

Situation: the application emits structured logs — request logs, business events, errors, audit entries — that need durable storage, fast time-range search, and retention policies. The volume is high (thousands per second at peak), and the app team wants log queries from MongoDB without standing up a separate observability stack.

Approach: use a time-series collection for raw logs with TTL-based retention; structure log documents with consistent fields (level, ts, service, message, context); index aggressively on the metaField (service, level); offload long-term archival to S3 via Online Archive or scheduled $out. For real-time dashboards, run rollups.

// Time-series log collection with auto-retention
db.createCollection("logs", {
  timeseries: {
    timeField: "ts",
    metaField: "meta",
    granularity: "seconds"
  },
  expireAfterSeconds: 30 * 86400   // 30-day retention
})

db.logs.insertOne({
  ts: new Date(),
  meta: { service: "checkout", env: "prod", level: "error", host: "checkout-7" },
  message: "payment_failed",
  request_id: "req_01HRG...",
  user_id: ObjectId("..."),
  context: {
    order_id: ObjectId("..."),
    amount_cents: 4999,
    error_code: "card_declined",
    stripe_intent: "pi_..."
  },
  duration_ms: 1842,
  http: { method: "POST", path: "/api/checkout", status: 500 }
})

// Common queries
// Recent errors for a service
db.logs.find({
  "meta.service": "checkout",
  "meta.level": "error",
  ts: { $gte: oneHourAgo }
}).sort({ ts: -1 }).limit(100)

// Trace by request_id
db.logs.find({ request_id: "req_01HRG..." }).sort({ ts: 1 })

// Error rate by minute (rollup)
db.logs.aggregate([
  { $match: { "meta.level": "error", ts: { $gte: oneHourAgo } } },
  { $group: {
      _id: {
        minute:  { $dateTrunc: { date: "$ts", unit: "minute" } },
        service: "$meta.service"
      },
      count: { $sum: 1 }
  }},
  { $merge: {
      into: "log_rollups_minute",
      on: "_id",
      whenMatched: "replace",
      whenNotMatched: "insert"
  }}
])

// Indexes — metaField fields are indexed automatically; add for hot queries
db.logs.createIndex({ "meta.level": 1, "meta.service": 1, ts: -1 })
db.logs.createIndex({ request_id: 1 })

Trade-offs:

DecisionWhyAlternative
Time-series collection10x compression, optimized for appendRegular collection — 10x storage cost
TTL retentionAuto-delete old logs; compliance-safeManual purge — forgotten data
Structured log fieldsIndexable; queryable; analyzableFree text — only grep works
Rollups for dashboardsSub-ms metric queriesLive aggregation — cluster pain at peak
MongoDB as logging backendOne stack to operate; Atlas Search for free-textSpecialized logging — better tooling but separate ops

Production polish: at >10K logs/sec, MongoDB’s time-series is fine but specialized logging stacks shine — Datadog, New Relic, Grafana Loki, Honeycomb, Better Stack, Axiom; structured logging libraries: pino/winston (Node), structlog/loguru (Python), tracing (Rust), logrus/zap (Go) — emit JSON, never strings; request_id generated at ingress and propagated via OpenTelemetry headers; distributed tracing via OpenTelemetry + Jaeger/Tempo/Honeycomb for cross-service correlation — logs reference trace_id; log scrubbing: PII filters at the application layer (passwords, credit cards) before write; archival to Atlas Online Archive or scheduled $out to S3 in Parquet format readable by Athena/Snowflake; alerting on error rate spikes via Datadog Monitors/PagerDuty; full-text search via Atlas Search for grep-like queries on message text; cost control: log sampling for high-volume info logs (1% sampled), full retention for warn/error.

Question 62

Explain how you would design a schema for a peer-to-peer lending platform with lenders, borrowers, and loans.

Situation: a peer-to-peer lending platform with lenders, borrowers, and loans. Borrowers post loan requests; lenders fund (often fractionally, splitting risk across many loans); repayments arrive monthly and are distributed across lenders. Compliance: KYC/AML, audit trails, regulatory reporting.

Approach: five collections. users with role flags (lender/borrower); loan_requests are the marketplace listings; loans are funded contracts; investments are per-lender stakes (one loan has many investments); payments are the immutable ledger of inflows/outflows. Money math uses Decimal128; transactions enforce atomicity.

// users (single collection, role flags)
db.users.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  email: "alice@example.com",
  roles: ["lender"],
  kyc: { status: "verified", provider: "persona", verified_at: new Date() },
  funding_account: { stripe_customer: "cus_...", balance_cents: 0 }
})

// loan_requests — the marketplace
db.loan_requests.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  borrower_id: ObjectId("..."),
  amount_cents: 1_000_000,                      // $10,000
  term_months: 36,
  apr_bps: 1199,                                // 11.99%
  purpose: "debt_consolidation",
  credit_grade: "B",
  funded_cents: 0,                               // denormalized
  status: "open",                                // open | funding | funded | rejected | expired
  expires_at: ISODate("..."),
  created_at: new Date()
})

// loans — funded contract
db.loans.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  request_id: ObjectId("..."),
  borrower_id: ObjectId("..."),
  principal_cents: 1_000_000,
  apr_bps: 1199,
  term_months: 36,
  monthly_payment_cents: 33_214,
  outstanding_principal_cents: 1_000_000,
  status: "active",                              // active | paid_off | charged_off | default
  funded_at: new Date(),
  next_payment_at: ISODate("...")
})

// investments — per-lender fractional stakes
db.investments.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  lender_id: ObjectId("..."),
  loan_id:   ObjectId("..."),
  amount_cents: 25_000,                          // $250 stake
  fraction_bps: 250,                              // 2.5% of the loan
  invested_at: new Date()
})

// payments — append-only ledger
db.payments.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  loan_id: ObjectId("..."),
  type: "borrower_payment",                       // borrower_payment | lender_distribution | fee
  amount_cents: 33_214,
  principal_cents: 27_550,
  interest_cents:  5_664,
  ts: new Date(),
  external_ref: "ach_..."
})

// Atomic funding (a lender invests $250 in a loan request)
const session = client.startSession()
await session.withTransaction(async () => {
  const result = await db.loan_requests.updateOne(
    { _id: requestId, status: "open",
      $expr: { $lte: [{ $add: ["$funded_cents", 25_000] }, "$amount_cents"] } },
    { $inc: { funded_cents: 25_000 } },
    { session }
  )
  if (result.modifiedCount === 0) throw new Error("oversubscribed")
  await db.investments.insertOne({ /* ... */ }, { session })
  await db.users.updateOne({ _id: lenderId },
    { $inc: { "funding_account.balance_cents": -25_000 } }, { session })
})

// Indexes
db.loan_requests.createIndex({ status: 1, credit_grade: 1, expires_at: 1 })
db.investments.createIndex({ lender_id: 1, invested_at: -1 })
db.investments.createIndex({ loan_id: 1 })
db.payments.createIndex({ loan_id: 1, ts: -1 })

Trade-offs:

DecisionWhyAlternative
Append-only payment ledgerAudit trail, regulatory requirementMutable balances — impossible to reconcile
Separate loan_requests & loansMarketplace lifecycle separate from funded contractsSingle doc with status — over-broad indexes
Fractional investments collectionMany lenders per loan, distributions atomicEmbed in loan — doc grows, write contention
Denormalized funded_centsMarketplace shows progress in O(1)Live $sum — expensive on hot loans
Transactions for fundingNo oversubscription; balance and investment in syncEventually consistent — legally risky

Production polish: KYC/AML via Persona/Onfido/Sumsub/Alloy with sanctions screening; payments and ACH via Stripe/Plaid/Modern Treasury/Increase; credit data from Experian/Equifax/TransUnion via Plaid; regulatory reporting (Consumer Financial Protection Bureau, SEC, state lending authorities) requires versioned records and 7+ year retention — never delete; amortization schedules generated and stored; delinquency workflows auto-charge late fees, escalate to collections via TrueAccord/Phin; tax reporting (1099-INT for interest income) generated annually via warehouse aggregations; ledger truthfulness: nightly job recomputes loan outstanding from payments and reconciles, alerts on drift; distributed-systems-grade money math: never use floats, always Decimal128 for fractional amounts; fraud detection via Sift/Sardine; change streams trigger lender notifications on borrower payments; compliance evidence via Drata/Vanta; double-entry accounting using a dedicated ledger like Tigerbeetle/Tinybook for the strictest financial environments.

Question 63

You are asked to design a database for a real estate platform with properties, agents, and listings. How would you structure the collections?

Situation: a real estate platform with properties, agents, and listings. Buyers search by location, price range, beds/baths, and features; agents manage their listings and leads; listings have rich media (photos, video tours, floor plans). Listings expire and get re-listed; price changes need history.

Approach: three collections. properties hold canonical property data (address, location, structural details that don’t change). listings are time-bound sales/rental events on a property — one property can have many listings over the years. agents hold agent profiles. Geospatial index on property location; price-history embedded in listings.

// properties — the building/parcel
db.properties.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  address: { line1: "123 Main St", city: "Austin", state: "TX", zip: "78701" },
  location: { type: "Point", coordinates: [-97.7431, 30.2672] },
  property_type: "single_family",
  beds: 4,
  baths: 2.5,
  sqft: 2_400,
  lot_sqft: 8_500,
  year_built: 2008,
  features: ["pool", "garage_2car", "fireplace"],
  apn: "0123456789",                       // assessor parcel number
  schools: { elementary: "Austin ISD - Hill ES", rating: 8 }
})

// listings — transactional events on the property
db.listings.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  property_id: ObjectId("..."),
  agent_id:    ObjectId("..."),
  type: "sale",                              // sale | rent | lease
  status: "active",                           // active | pending | sold | expired | withdrawn
  list_price_cents: 92_500_000,
  current_price_cents: 89_500_000,            // after a reduction
  price_history: [
    { ts: ISODate("2026-04-01"), price_cents: 92_500_000, change: "initial" },
    { ts: ISODate("2026-04-22"), price_cents: 89_500_000, change: "reduction" }
  ],
  description: "Beautifully renovated...",
  media: {
    photos: ["s3://...img1.jpg", "..."],
    virtual_tour_url: "https://...",
    floor_plans: ["s3://..."]
  },
  listed_at: ISODate("2026-04-01"),
  expires_at: ISODate("2026-10-01"),
  views: 0,                                  // denormalized
  saves: 0,
  showings_scheduled: 0
})

// agents
db.agents.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  user_id: ObjectId("..."),
  license: { state: "TX", number: "TX12345", expires: ISODate("2027-12-31") },
  brokerage: "Realty Partners",
  bio: "...",
  rating: 4.8,
  active_listings_count: 0
})

// Common search: 3+ beds, $500K-$1M, near Austin downtown
db.listings.aggregate([
  { $match: { status: "active", type: "sale",
              current_price_cents: { $gte: 500_000_00, $lte: 1_000_000_00 } } },
  { $lookup: {
      from: "properties",
      localField: "property_id", foreignField: "_id",
      as: "property"
  }},
  { $unwind: "$property" },
  { $match: { "property.beds": { $gte: 3 } } },
  { $geoNear: {       // place this earlier ideally
      near: { type: "Point", coordinates: [-97.74, 30.27] },
      distanceField: "property.distance",
      key: "property.location",
      maxDistance: 10_000,
      spherical: true
  }},
  { $sort: { listed_at: -1 } },
  { $limit: 50 }
])

// Indexes
db.properties.createIndex({ location: "2dsphere" })
db.properties.createIndex({ "address.zip": 1 })
db.listings.createIndex({ status: 1, type: 1, current_price_cents: 1 })
db.listings.createIndex({ property_id: 1, listed_at: -1 })
db.listings.createIndex({ agent_id: 1, status: 1 })

Trade-offs:

DecisionWhyAlternative
Property + listing splitSame house relisted; track sale history per propertySingle doc — rewrites “property” on every relist
Embedded price_historyAlways read with listing; bounded sizeSeparate collection — extra $lookup
2dsphere on propertyMap-based search; “near my office”City filter — misses suburbs
Snapshot agent_id at listing timeListing survives agent changesReference current agent — broken on relist
Status field, no deletesAudit trail, MLS complianceHard delete — lost history

Production polish: ingest MLS data via Bridge Interactive/RESO Web API/Trestle; Atlas Search powers fuzzy address search and feature search; property images via Cloudinary/imgix with auto-WebP; virtual tours via Matterport/Zillow 3D Home; school data from GreatSchools API; walk scores from Walk Score API; lead capture via integrated forms with anti-spam (hCaptcha/Cloudflare Turnstile); showing scheduling integrated with Calendly/ShowingTime; document signing via DocuSign/Dropbox Sign; analytics dashboards for agents (views/saves/leads per listing) via Atlas Charts; sold price history exposed for comp analysis — valuable for buyers; fair-housing compliance — certain demographic targeting forbidden, audit trails on filters; email digests (new listings matching saved search) via Customer.io/Iterable; mortgage pre-qualification via Plaid/Lendi; map tiles via Mapbox/MapTiler; change streams notify saved-search subscribers when matching listings appear or drop in price.

Question 64

How would you handle data synchronization between MongoDB and other databases or services?

Situation: MongoDB serves the OLTP application but data must be replicated to other systems — a data warehouse for analytics, a search engine for discovery, a cache for hot reads, a CRM for customer support. Some destinations need near-real-time updates; others tolerate batch refresh.

Approach: use the right tool per destination. Change streams stream individual document changes to message buses (Kafka, Redpanda) and downstream consumers in near real time. Scheduled batch ETL via Airbyte/Fivetran/Estuary handles warehouses every 5-60 minutes. Dual-write within a transaction handles same-DB mirrors.

// Pattern 1: Change streams → Kafka → many consumers
const stream = db.collection("orders").watch([], {
  fullDocument: "updateLookup",
  fullDocumentBeforeChange: "whenAvailable"
})

for await (const change of stream) {
  await kafka.produce({
    topic: "orders.changes",
    key: String(change.documentKey._id),
    value: JSON.stringify({
      operation: change.operationType,    // insert | update | delete | replace
      document_id: change.documentKey._id,
      full_document: change.fullDocument,
      before: change.fullDocumentBeforeChange,
      cluster_time: change.clusterTime,
      resume_token: change._id
    })
  })
  await persistResumeToken(change._id)
}

// Consumer 1: Update Algolia search index
async function syncToAlgolia(event) {
  if (event.operation === "delete") return algolia.deleteObject(event.document_id)
  return algolia.saveObject({ ...event.full_document, objectID: event.full_document._id })
}

// Consumer 2: Invalidate Redis cache
async function invalidateCache(event) {
  await redis.del(`order:${event.document_id}`)
}

// Consumer 3: Update CRM (Salesforce / HubSpot)
async function syncToCRM(event) { /* ... */ }

// Pattern 2: Batch sync to warehouse via Airbyte / Fivetran
// Configured outside MongoDB — runs hourly, full-refresh or CDC

// Pattern 3: Two-phase write inside a transaction (DB-to-DB mirror)
const session = client.startSession()
await session.withTransaction(async () => {
  await primary.collection("users").insertOne(user, { session })
  await replica.collection("users_audit").insertOne({
    _id: user._id, action: "create", user, ts: new Date()
  }, { session })
})

Trade-offs:

DecisionWhyAlternative
Change streams + KafkaOne CDC source, infinite consumers; replay capabilityPer-consumer change stream — oplog pressure, no replay
Resume tokens persistedRecover from worker crash without lost eventsStart-from-now — missed events during downtime
Batch ETL for warehouseCost-efficient; row-store → column-store transformReal-time CDC into warehouse — expensive, often unnecessary
Idempotent consumersSafe redelivery after failureNon-idempotent — double-applies on retry
Transactions for tightly coupled writesStrong consistency for audits / mirrorsBest-effort — drift, alerts at 3am

Production polish: use Debezium MongoDB connector as the CDC bridge to Kafka/Redpanda/AWS MSK/Confluent Cloud — battle-tested, handles schema evolution, exactly-once semantics; warehouse ETL via Fivetran/Airbyte/Estuary Flow/Stitch/Hevo with destinations BigQuery/Snowflake/Databricks/ClickHouse/Tinybird; reverse-ETL (warehouse → SaaS) via Hightouch/Census for marketing tools; search indexes via Atlas Search (built-in, no sync needed), Elasticsearch/OpenSearch, Algolia, Meilisearch, Typesense; cache layer via Redis/Dragonfly/KeyDB; monitoring: lag metrics on every consumer (resume token age vs $$NOW) alerting in Datadog/Grafana; reconciliation jobs hourly count source vs destination, alert on drift; backfill: when starting a new consumer, snapshot existing data once, then resume from current change stream position; schema registry via Confluent Schema Registry ensures consumers handle schema evolution; data quality checks via Soda/Great Expectations/Monte Carlo.

Question 65

Describe how you would implement a schema for a freelance marketplace with freelancers, clients, and projects.

Situation: a freelance marketplace with freelancers, clients, and projects. Freelancers post profiles and bid on projects; clients post projects and review proposals; payment is held in escrow and released on milestones; reviews and reputation drive matchmaking.

Approach: five collections. users with role flags; projects the marketplace listings; proposals bids on projects; contracts active engagements with milestones; reviews bidirectional ratings. Escrow handled by Stripe Connect or specialized payments; the database tracks state but money lives at the payment provider.

// users (role flags)
db.users.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  email: "alice@example.com",
  roles: ["freelancer"],
  freelancer: {
    headline: "Full-stack engineer",
    skills: ["mongodb", "node", "react"],
    hourly_rate_cents: 8_500,
    bio: "...",
    portfolio: ["https://...", "..."],
    rating: 4.9,
    completed_jobs: 47
  },
  client: null,
  stripe_account: { connected: true, account_id: "acct_..." }
})

// projects — marketplace listings
db.projects.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  client_id: ObjectId("..."),
  title: "Build MongoDB-backed dashboard",
  description: "...",
  category: "web_development",
  skills_required: ["mongodb", "react", "atlas_charts"],
  budget: { type: "fixed", amount_cents: 500_000 },   // or { type: "hourly", min: ..., max: ... }
  duration: "1_to_3_months",
  status: "open",                                       // open | in_review | awarded | in_progress | completed | cancelled
  proposal_count: 0,                                    // denormalized
  created_at: new Date(),
  expires_at: ISODate("...")
})

// proposals
db.proposals.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  project_id: ObjectId("..."),
  freelancer_id: ObjectId("..."),
  cover_letter: "...",
  bid: { type: "fixed", amount_cents: 480_000 },
  estimated_duration_days: 45,
  status: "submitted",        // submitted | shortlisted | rejected | withdrawn | accepted
  submitted_at: new Date()
})

// contracts — with milestones
db.contracts.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  project_id:    ObjectId("..."),
  client_id:     ObjectId("..."),
  freelancer_id: ObjectId("..."),
  amount_cents:  480_000,
  milestones: [
    { _id: "m1", title: "Setup & auth",       amount_cents: 100_000, status: "released",
      escrowed_at: ISODate("..."), released_at: ISODate("...") },
    { _id: "m2", title: "Core features",       amount_cents: 240_000, status: "in_escrow",
      escrowed_at: ISODate("..."), released_at: null },
    { _id: "m3", title: "Polish & deployment",  amount_cents: 140_000, status: "pending" }
  ],
  status: "active",   // active | completed | cancelled | disputed
  started_at: new Date()
})

// reviews
db.reviews.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  contract_id: ObjectId("..."),
  reviewer_id: ObjectId("..."),
  reviewee_id: ObjectId("..."),
  reviewer_role: "client",
  rating: 5,
  comment: "Outstanding work, communication, and delivery.",
  created_at: new Date()
})

// Indexes
db.projects.createIndex({ status: 1, skills_required: 1, created_at: -1 })
db.proposals.createIndex({ project_id: 1, status: 1 })
db.proposals.createIndex({ freelancer_id: 1, submitted_at: -1 })
db.contracts.createIndex({ freelancer_id: 1, status: 1 })
db.contracts.createIndex({ client_id: 1, status: 1 })
db.reviews.createIndex({ reviewee_id: 1, created_at: -1 })

Trade-offs:

DecisionWhyAlternative
Single users with role flagsSame person can be both client and freelancerSeparate collections — identity duplication
Embedded milestones in contractAlways read together; bounded sizeSeparate collection — extra $lookup
Snapshot rates/skills at contract timeEngagement survives profile changesReference live profile — rewrites history
Stripe Connect for escrowCompliance offloaded; payouts handledCustom escrow — regulated, capital intensive
Bidirectional reviewsBoth parties build reputationOne-way — clients abuse freelancers

Production polish: escrow and split payouts via Stripe Connect (Standard or Express accounts); tax forms (1099-NEC for US freelancers, W-8BEN international) via Stripe Tax/Bench/Track1099; identity verification via Persona/Onfido/Stripe Identity; dispute resolution workflow with mediator role and held funds; messaging between client and freelancer via WebSockets (Stream Chat/Sendbird/Pusher); file sharing via S3 with virus scanning (ClamAV); matching algorithm uses Atlas Vector Search on skill+description embeddings; fraud detection: account farms, collusion, fake reviews via Sift/Sardine + behavioral analytics; contract templates with e-signing via DocuSign/Dropbox Sign; time tracking for hourly contracts via Toggl/Harvest integrations; review moderation via Perspective API/Hive for toxicity; discovery: featured/promoted listings via boost field, paid promotions; change streams trigger lifecycle events — new proposals notify clients, accepted proposals create contracts; analytics in Atlas Charts/Metabase.

Question 66

You need to design a database for a conference management system with events, speakers, and attendees. How would you structure the collections?

Situation: a conference management system with events, speakers, sessions, and attendees. Events have call-for-papers, ticketed registration, multiple session tracks, scheduled talks. Attendees register, build a personal agenda, and check in on-site. Reads spike massively the week of the conference.

Approach: five collections. events hold conference metadata. sessions are individual talks scheduled in tracks/rooms. speakers link to user accounts (one person can speak at many events). tickets track registration and check-in. agendas are per-attendee saved schedules. Heavy read caching for the schedule page; transactions only on ticket purchase.

// events
db.events.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  name: "MongoDB World 2026",
  slug: "mongodb-world-2026",
  starts_at: ISODate("2026-06-20T09:00:00Z"),
  ends_at:   ISODate("2026-06-22T18:00:00Z"),
  venue: {
    name: "Javits Center", city: "NYC",
    location: { type: "Point", coordinates: [-74.003, 40.756] }
  },
  capacity: 5_000,
  ticket_tiers: [
    { _id: "early", name: "Early Bird", price_cents: 89900, sold: 0,
      limit: 1_000, sales_end: ISODate("2026-04-01") },
    { _id: "regular", name: "Regular", price_cents: 129900, sold: 0,
      limit: 4_000, sales_end: ISODate("2026-06-15") }
  ],
  status: "published"
})

// sessions
db.sessions.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  event_id: ObjectId("..."),
  title: "Sharding at Petabyte Scale",
  abstract: "...",
  speakers: [
    { user_id: ObjectId("..."), name: "Alice Cole", company: "Acme Corp" }
  ],
  starts_at: ISODate("2026-06-20T11:00:00Z"),
  duration_minutes: 45,
  track: "Architecture",
  room: "Hall 4A",
  capacity: 400,
  level: "advanced",
  tags: ["sharding", "scale"],
  status: "confirmed"
})

// tickets
db.tickets.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  event_id: ObjectId("..."),
  user_id: ObjectId("..."),
  tier_id: "early",
  amount_paid_cents: 89900,
  qr_code: "TKT-01HRG...",
  checked_in_at: null,
  payment: { provider: "stripe", intent_id: "pi_..." },
  purchased_at: new Date()
})

// agendas (saved sessions per attendee)
db.agendas.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  user_id: ObjectId("..."),
  event_id: ObjectId("..."),
  saved_session_ids: [ObjectId("..."), ObjectId("...")],
  updated_at: new Date()
})

// Atomic ticket purchase
const session = client.startSession()
await session.withTransaction(async () => {
  const r = await db.events.updateOne(
    { _id: eventId, "ticket_tiers._id": "early",
      $expr: { $lt: [
        { $arrayElemAt: ["$ticket_tiers.sold", { $indexOfArray: ["$ticket_tiers._id", "early"] }] },
        { $arrayElemAt: ["$ticket_tiers.limit", { $indexOfArray: ["$ticket_tiers._id", "early"] }] }
      ]}
    },
    { $inc: { "ticket_tiers.$.sold": 1 } },
    { session }
  )
  if (r.modifiedCount === 0) throw new Error("sold_out")
  await db.tickets.insertOne({ /* ... */ }, { session })
})

// Check in (on-site, scan QR)
db.tickets.updateOne(
  { qr_code, checked_in_at: null },
  { $set: { checked_in_at: new Date() } }
)

// Indexes
db.sessions.createIndex({ event_id: 1, starts_at: 1 })
db.sessions.createIndex({ event_id: 1, track: 1 })
db.tickets.createIndex({ qr_code: 1 }, { unique: true })
db.tickets.createIndex({ user_id: 1, event_id: 1 })
db.agendas.createIndex({ user_id: 1, event_id: 1 }, { unique: true })

Trade-offs:

DecisionWhyAlternative
Embedded ticket tiers in eventBounded (5-10 tiers); always read with eventSeparate collection — extra round trip
Snapshot speaker name/company on sessionSpeaker profile changes don’t rewrite sessionLive $lookup — latency on schedule page
Conditional inc with limit checkAtomic sell-out enforcementRead-then-write — race conditions on early bird
Per-user agendas collectionSaved sessions independent of ticketsEmbed in user — doc grows unboundedly
QR codes on ticketsFast on-site check-in via mobile scanLookup-by-name — bottleneck at door

Production polish: ticketing via Stripe Checkout with Apple Pay/Google Pay; schedule rendering heavily cached — static export to Vercel/Cloudflare Pages, ISR-revalidated on session change via change streams; conflict detection in agenda — warn when saved sessions overlap; session recommendations via Atlas Vector Search on attendee role + interests; QR code generation with anti-replay (HMAC-signed payload, single-use); on-site check-in apps built with React Native or PWA, offline-first via IndexedDB sync; live updates (room changes, cancellations) push to attendee phones via OneSignal/Firebase; networking features (1:1 meeting requests) need a separate meetings collection; sponsor exhibits with lead-scan tracking; swag/perks redeemable per ticket; video for hybrid events via Mux/Vimeo/YouTube Live; post-event: session recordings published, attendee certificates, analytics dashboards; compliance: GDPR opt-in for marketing, data retention policies, accessibility (alt text, transcripts); email automation via Customer.io/Iterable for pre/during/post-event journeys; SMS reminders via Twilio.

Question 67

How would you implement a feature that tracks user engagement and activity metrics in MongoDB?

Situation: the product team needs user engagement metrics — daily active users (DAU/MAU), feature usage, retention curves, funnel completion rates, session duration. Events fire from web, mobile, and backend; the analytics layer must serve dashboards in seconds and never cause OLTP slowdown.

Approach: emit a standardized event schema from the application; capture into a time-series collection; aggregate to materialized rollups (DAU, MAU, feature counts) via scheduled $merge pipelines; expose dashboards from the rollups, never from raw events. For deep funnels and cohorts, export to a warehouse.

// Time-series events
db.createCollection("user_events", {
  timeseries: { timeField: "ts", metaField: "meta", granularity: "seconds" },
  expireAfterSeconds: 90 * 86400      // 90-day raw retention
})

db.user_events.insertOne({
  ts: new Date(),
  meta: {
    user_id: ObjectId("..."),
    event: "feature_used",
    platform: "ios",
    app_version: "8.4.1",
    country: "US"
  },
  properties: {
    feature: "search_v2",
    duration_ms: 450,
    result_count: 12
  },
  session_id: "sess_01HRG...",
  device_id: "dev_..."
})

// Daily Active Users (DAU)
db.user_events.aggregate([
  { $match: { ts: { $gte: yesterday, $lt: today } } },
  { $group: {
      _id: {
        date: { $dateTrunc: { date: "$ts", unit: "day" } }
      },
      dau:        { $addToSet: "$meta.user_id" }
  }},
  { $set: { dau_count: { $size: "$dau" } } },
  { $unset: "dau" },
  { $merge: "metrics_daily" }
])

// Feature usage by minute
db.user_events.aggregate([
  { $match: { "meta.event": "feature_used", ts: { $gte: oneHourAgo } } },
  { $group: {
      _id: {
        minute: { $dateTrunc: { date: "$ts", unit: "minute" } },
        feature: "$properties.feature"
      },
      uses: { $sum: 1 },
      unique_users: { $addToSet: "$meta.user_id" }
  }},
  { $set: { unique_users: { $size: "$unique_users" } } },
  { $merge: "feature_usage_minute" }
])

// 7-day retention — users active on day 7 after install
db.user_events.aggregate([
  { $match: { "meta.event": "session_start", ts: { $gte: sevenDaysAgo } } },
  { $group: {
      _id: "$meta.user_id",
      first_session: { $min: "$ts" },
      last_session:  { $max: "$ts" }
  }},
  { $match: {
      first_session: { $gte: cohortStart, $lt: cohortEnd },
      $expr: { $gte: ["$last_session", { $add: ["$first_session", 7*86400000] }] }
  }},
  { $count: "retained" }
])

// Indexes (metaField fields auto-indexed in time-series collections)
db.user_events.createIndex({ "meta.event": 1, "meta.user_id": 1, ts: -1 })

Trade-offs:

DecisionWhyAlternative
Time-series collection10x compression on event dataRegular collection — storage explodes
Materialized rollupsDashboards load in O(rollup count)Live aggregation — minutes per refresh
Standardized event schemaConsistent fields across platformsFree-form — messy, hard to analyze
90-day raw retention + permanent rollupsStorage bounded; trends preservedForever raw — expensive; metrics-only — can’t reanalyze
Dual-track: rollups + warehouseFast dashboards; deep cohort analysisMongo only — struggles with complex SQL analytics

Production polish: for serious product analytics use specialized tools — Mixpanel, Amplitude, PostHog, Heap, June; they handle funnels, cohorts, retention curves, A/B tests, and feature flags out of the box; if MongoDB is the source of truth, pipe events to Segment/RudderStack for fan-out to all destinations; warehouse export via Airbyte/Fivetran/Estuary to BigQuery/Snowflake/Databricks/ClickHouse/Tinybird; real-time dashboards in Atlas Charts, Metabase, Hex, Lightdash, Cube; privacy: PII fields excluded from events (use user_id, never email); consent tracked — respect GDPR/CCPA opt-outs; event taxonomy documented in a single registry (Notion, Tracking Plan); schema evolution: validators on event collection prevent drift; session stitching: assign session_id on session_start, reuse for ~30 min idle window; experimentation via Statsig/LaunchDarkly/GrowthBook/Eppo; alerting on metric anomalies via Datadog/Anomaly; aggregation jobs orchestrated via BullMQ/Inngest/Trigger.dev/Temporal.

Question 68

Explain how you would design a schema for a dating app with users, profiles, and matches.

Situation: a dating app with users, profiles, and matches. Profiles include photos, prompts, preferences (age range, distance, gender). The matching engine surfaces candidate profiles per user; mutual likes create matches; matches enable messaging. Privacy and abuse prevention are first-class concerns.

Approach: separate users from profiles for security; actions (like/pass) is an append-only ledger; matches is the materialized list of mutual likes; messages belong to a match. Geospatial index on profile location; per-pair uniqueness in actions; transactions for the like-creates-match flow.

// users (auth identity)
db.users.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  email: "alice@example.com",
  phone: "+1-555-0123",
  email_verified: true,
  phone_verified: true,
  account_status: "active",      // active | paused | banned
  created_at: new Date()
})

// profiles (public-ish persona)
db.profiles.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  user_id: ObjectId("..."),
  display_name: "Alice",
  age: 32,                         // computed daily from dob
  gender: "female",
  pronouns: ["she", "her"],
  bio: "Coffee, books, hiking...",
  photos: [
    { url: "s3://...", verified: true, primary: true }
  ],
  prompts: [
    { question: "I'm looking for...", answer: "..." }
  ],
  location: { type: "Point", coordinates: [-73.985, 40.748] },
  city: "Brooklyn, NY",
  preferences: {
    seeking: ["male"],
    age_range: [28, 38],
    max_distance_km: 25
  },
  visibility: "public",            // public | hidden | paused
  last_active: new Date()
})

// actions — append-only swipe ledger
db.actions.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  actor_id:  ObjectId("..."),
  target_id: ObjectId("..."),
  action: "like",                  // like | super_like | pass
  ts: new Date()
})
db.actions.createIndex({ actor_id: 1, target_id: 1 }, { unique: true })
db.actions.createIndex({ target_id: 1, action: 1, ts: -1 })

// matches — mutual likes
db.matches.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  participants: [ObjectId("..."), ObjectId("...")].sort(),  // sorted for uniqueness
  created_at: new Date(),
  unmatched_at: null,
  last_message_at: null
})
db.matches.createIndex({ participants: 1, created_at: -1 })
db.matches.createIndex({ participants: 1 }, { unique: true })

// Like + match-creation in a transaction
const session = client.startSession()
await session.withTransaction(async () => {
  await db.actions.insertOne({ actor_id, target_id, action: "like", ts: new Date() }, { session })
  // Did the target like us first?
  const reciprocal = await db.actions.findOne(
    { actor_id: target_id, target_id: actor_id, action: { $in: ["like", "super_like"] } },
    { session }
  )
  if (reciprocal) {
    await db.matches.insertOne({
      participants: [actor_id, target_id].sort(),
      created_at: new Date()
    }, { session })
  }
})

// Discover profiles (filter + geo)
db.profiles.aggregate([
  { $geoNear: {
      near: { type: "Point", coordinates: [myLng, myLat] },
      distanceField: "distance_km",
      maxDistance: 25_000,
      spherical: true,
      query: {
        gender: { $in: myPrefs.seeking },
        age: { $gte: myPrefs.age_range[0], $lte: myPrefs.age_range[1] },
        visibility: "public",
        user_id: { $nin: alreadyActedOn }
      }
  }},
  { $limit: 50 }
])

Trade-offs:

DecisionWhyAlternative
Users + profiles splitAuth fields stay private; profile is sharedSingle doc — PII leaks risk
Append-only actions ledgerAudit, prevent re-swipes, abuse detectionMutate state — lose history
Materialized matchesInbox loads in O(1)Live join on every action — expensive
Sorted participants arrayUnique pair regardless of orderTwo rows per match — duplication
Transaction for like + matchNo race when both swipe simultaneouslyEventually consistent — missed matches

Production polish: photo verification (selfie matching profile photo) via Persona/Onfido/Microsoft Cognitive Services Face API; abuse and harassment detection via Hive/Sift/Perspective API for messages and image moderation; safety features — report flow, block list (mutual hide), panic button, location obfuscation (show distance not exact location); rate limiting on actions to detect bots; messaging via Stream Chat/Sendbird/PubNub with E2E encryption optional; video calls via Daily.co/LiveKit/Agora; matchmaking algorithm: collaborative filtering (Atlas Vector Search on profile embeddings) + recency signals + diversity guards; premium tiers (Tinder Gold/Hinge+) via Stripe Billing/RevenueCat for IAP; change streams on matches trigger push notifications via OneSignal/Firebase; compliance: age verification (18+), GDPR/CCPA data export and deletion, retention policies, COPPA absolute floor; analytics via Mixpanel/Amplitude for funnel optimization; fraud rings detection via graph patterns (one device, many accounts) — Sardine/Sift/Forter; trust & safety team workflow on flagged content via Linear/Zendesk.

Question 69

You are asked to design a database for a digital library with books, authors, and borrowers. How would you structure the collections?

Situation: a digital library with books, authors, and borrowers. Books may have multiple copies/licenses (concurrent borrowing limits); borrowers check out for finite periods; holds queue when copies are unavailable; reading progress synced across devices. The collection grows but is bounded (catalog size, not infinite events).

Approach: four collections. books (canonical metadata) authors (people) licenses (ownership records, one row per copy or one row per concurrent-license-pool), loans (active and historical checkouts). holds queues users for unavailable books. reading_progress tracks per-user-per-book position.

// authors
db.authors.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  name: "Jane Doe",
  bio: "...",
  born: ISODate("1965-03-22"),
  nationality: "US"
})

// books — canonical
db.books.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  isbn: "978-0-13-468599-1",
  title: "MongoDB at Scale",
  authors: [
    { author_id: ObjectId("..."), name: "Jane Doe" }       // snapshotted name
  ],
  publisher: "Tech Press",
  publish_date: ISODate("2024-09-15"),
  language: "en",
  cover_url: "https://cdn.../cover.jpg",
  description: "...",
  categories: ["technology", "databases"],
  format: "ebook",                                          // ebook | audiobook
  pages: 412,
  drm: "adobe_acsm"
})

// licenses — concurrent-borrow capacity
db.licenses.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  book_id:        ObjectId("..."),
  total_copies:   25,
  available_copies: 22,                                     // denormalized
  publisher_terms: { metered: false, expires: null }
})

// loans
db.loans.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  book_id:    ObjectId("..."),
  user_id:    ObjectId("..."),
  checked_out_at: new Date(),
  due_at:        ISODate("2026-05-13"),                     // 14 days
  returned_at: null,
  status: "active"                                          // active | returned | overdue
})

// holds (queue when unavailable)
db.holds.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  book_id: ObjectId("..."),
  user_id: ObjectId("..."),
  position: 4,                                              // queue position
  notified_at: null,
  expires_at: null
})

// reading_progress (synced across devices)
db.reading_progress.updateOne(
  { user_id: ObjectId("..."), book_id: ObjectId("...") },
  { $set: {
      cfi: "epubcfi(/6/14[chap03]!/4/2/14)",                // EPUB CFI position
      percent: 32,
      device: "ipad",
      updated_at: new Date()
  }}, { upsert: true }
)

// Atomic checkout
const session = client.startSession()
await session.withTransaction(async () => {
  const r = await db.licenses.updateOne(
    { book_id, available_copies: { $gte: 1 } },
    { $inc: { available_copies: -1 } },
    { session }
  )
  if (r.modifiedCount === 0) throw new Error("no_copies_available")
  await db.loans.insertOne({ /* ... */ }, { session })
})

// Return
const session2 = client.startSession()
await session2.withTransaction(async () => {
  await db.loans.updateOne({ _id: loanId }, { $set: { returned_at: new Date(), status: "returned" } }, { session: session2 })
  await db.licenses.updateOne({ book_id }, { $inc: { available_copies: 1 } }, { session: session2 })
})

// Indexes
db.books.createIndex({ isbn: 1 }, { unique: true })
db.books.createIndex({ "authors.author_id": 1 })
db.licenses.createIndex({ book_id: 1 }, { unique: true })
db.loans.createIndex({ user_id: 1, status: 1 })
db.loans.createIndex({ book_id: 1, status: 1 })
db.holds.createIndex({ book_id: 1, position: 1 })

Trade-offs:

DecisionWhyAlternative
Separate licenses from booksLicense terms change without rewriting book metadataEmbed in book — conflated concerns
Atomic dec with $gte: 1 filterNo oversell; concurrent checkout safeRead-then-write — classic race
Holds queue collectionFair scheduling, FIFO guaranteesNone — lost demand for popular books
Reading progress upsertOne doc per user-book; cross-device syncPer-device records — complicated merge
14-day fixed termSimple, matches library normsPer-book terms — admin overhead

Production polish: ebook DRM via Readium LCP/Adobe ACSM/Apple FairPlay/Amazon Kindle DRM; audiobook streaming via Mux/Cloudflare Stream; ebook reader via Readium SDK/Foliate-js/EPUB.js; file storage via S3/R2/B2; OPDS catalog feed for compatible reader apps; ISBN/metadata enrichment via Open Library API/Google Books API; publisher/aggregator integrations: OverDrive, Hoopla, cloudLibrary; auto-return: scheduled job at due_at sets returned + frees license; hold notifications: when copy becomes available, top of queue gets 24h to check out; recommendations via Atlas Vector Search on book descriptions and reading history; analytics: most-borrowed, time-on-page, completion rates exported to BigQuery/Snowflake; library card auth via SIP2/SIP3 protocols for institutional access; privacy — library reading history is sensitive (US: protected by state library privacy laws); change streams trigger reading-streak notifications via Customer.io; full-text search via Atlas Search with weighted title/author/description fields and synonyms.

Question 70

How would you handle database performance tuning and optimization for high-traffic applications?

Situation: a high-traffic application running on MongoDB shows degraded performance — slow queries, replica lag spikes, occasional connection errors, working set larger than RAM. The team must improve performance without rewriting the application.

Approach: systematic performance tuning across six areas: indexes (cover the slow queries), schema (avoid unbounded growth, match access patterns), query patterns (projection, batch, avoid scanned-not-returned), hardware (RAM for working set, NVMe disks), cluster topology (replica set sizing, sharding when appropriate), application layer (connection pooling, caching).

// 1. Identify slow queries
db.setProfilingLevel(1, { slowms: 100 })       // log queries > 100ms
db.system.profile.find().sort({ ts: -1 }).limit(20)

// Or use the Atlas Performance Advisor / mongotop / mongostat

// 2. Explain a slow query
db.orders.find({ user_id, status: "pending" }).sort({ created_at: -1 }).explain("executionStats")
// Look for: COLLSCAN, IXSCAN, totalDocsExamined vs nReturned, executionTimeMillis, in-memory SORT

// 3. Add covering indexes (ESR rule: Equality, Sort, Range)
db.orders.createIndex({ user_id: 1, status: 1, created_at: -1 })

// 4. Project only needed fields (cuts network + memory)
db.orders.find({ user_id }, { _id: 1, total: 1, status: 1, created_at: 1 })

// 5. Use $lookup pipeline form for filtered joins (5.0+)
db.orders.aggregate([
  { $match: { user_id } },
  { $lookup: {
      from: "products", localField: "items.product_id", foreignField: "_id",
      as: "products",
      pipeline: [{ $project: { name: 1, price_cents: 1 } }]   // smaller payload
  }}
])

// 6. Bulk operations
const ops = items.map(item => ({
  updateOne: { filter: { _id: item._id }, update: { $set: { ... } } }
}))
db.products.bulkWrite(ops, { ordered: false })

// 7. Read preference for analytics-style queries
db.orders.find({ ... }).readPref("secondaryPreferred", [{ workload: "analytics" }])

// 8. Enable index hints when the planner picks wrong
db.orders.find(query).hint({ user_id: 1, created_at: -1 })

// 9. Identify and remove unused indexes
db.orders.aggregate([{ $indexStats: {} }])    // accesses.ops shows usage

// 10. Connection pool tuning (Mongoose / driver level)
mongoose.connect(uri, { maxPoolSize: 100, minPoolSize: 10, maxIdleTimeMS: 30000 })

Trade-offs:

DecisionWhyAlternative
Profiler at slowms: 100Surfaces problems without overhead in prodOff — flying blind; on always — profile collection grows
ESR-aligned compound indexesCover query + avoid in-memory sortSingle-field indexes — intersection slower
Projections on hot queriesLess network, less RAM, less serializationFull doc — CPU and bandwidth wasted
Bulk writes10-100x throughput vs individual writesPer-op write — round-trip latency dominates
Drop unused indexesEach write maintains every index — smaller surface = faster writesKeep them — write amplification

Production polish: on MongoDB Atlas, use Performance Advisor — auto-recommends indexes from your slow query log; Atlas Query Insights shows query patterns and outliers; cluster sizing: working set must fit in RAM (use db.serverStatus().wiredTiger.cache stats), CPU sized for concurrent operations, IOPS sized for write rate; storage: NVMe SSDs with appropriate IOPS provisioning; caching layer: Redis/Dragonfly/KeyDB in front of MongoDB for hot reads (cache-aside or write-through); read scaling: secondary reads with appropriate staleness via readPreference: secondaryPreferred; sharding only when single-replica-set ceiling is hit and a good shard key exists; connection management: connection pool per app instance, not per request; schema patterns: avoid unbounded arrays (cap at ~hundreds), avoid deeply nested docs (paths require traversal); monitoring: Datadog/New Relic/Honeycomb/Percona PMM — alerts on p99 latency, connection saturation, replica lag, oplog window; load testing: k6/Artillery/locust with realistic data shapes before production; capacity planning: project growth quarterly, scale ahead of demand.

Question 71

Describe how you would implement a schema for a subscription-based service with plans, subscribers, and payments.

Situation: a subscription service (SaaS, streaming, newsletter, fitness app) with plans, subscribers, and recurring payments. Plans have tiers and billing cycles; subscribers upgrade/downgrade/cancel; failed charges enter dunning workflows. Compliance: tax, refunds, proration, audit.

Approach: never reinvent billing — let Stripe Billing/Chargebee/Recurly hold the canonical billing state and call your webhooks. MongoDB stores app-side context: plans (linked to provider IDs), subscriber state, entitlements (what features each tier unlocks), and invoice metadata. Webhooks update local state; the app reads local state for fast access checks.

// plans (linked to Stripe price IDs)
db.plans.insertOne({
  _id: "plan_pro",
  name: "Pro",
  stripe_price_id: "price_pro_monthly",
  amount_cents: 2900,
  interval: "month",
  features: ["unlimited_projects", "priority_support", "team_seats:10"],
  active: true
})

// subscribers (synced from Stripe via webhooks)
db.subscribers.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  user_id: ObjectId("..."),
  org_id:  ObjectId("..."),
  stripe_customer_id: "cus_...",
  stripe_subscription_id: "sub_...",
  plan_id: "plan_pro",
  status: "active",                            // trialing | active | past_due | canceled | incomplete
  current_period_start: ISODate("2026-04-01"),
  current_period_end:   ISODate("2026-05-01"),
  cancel_at_period_end: false,
  trial_ends_at: null,
  features_cache: ["unlimited_projects", "priority_support", "team_seats:10"]
})

// invoices (metadata only; Stripe is the source of truth)
db.invoices.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  stripe_invoice_id: "in_...",
  subscriber_id: ObjectId("..."),
  amount_due_cents: 2900,
  amount_paid_cents: 2900,
  status: "paid",                              // open | paid | void | uncollectible
  period_start: ISODate("..."),
  period_end:   ISODate("..."),
  pdf_url: "https://stripe.com/...",
  created_at: new Date()
})

// Webhook handler (Stripe signed)
async function handleStripeWebhook(event) {
  switch (event.type) {
    case "customer.subscription.created":
    case "customer.subscription.updated":
      const sub = event.data.object
      await db.subscribers.updateOne(
        { stripe_subscription_id: sub.id },
        { $set: {
            status: sub.status,
            plan_id: planIdFromPrice(sub.items.data[0].price.id),
            current_period_start: new Date(sub.current_period_start * 1000),
            current_period_end:   new Date(sub.current_period_end * 1000),
            cancel_at_period_end: sub.cancel_at_period_end,
            features_cache: featuresForPlan(planIdFromPrice(sub.items.data[0].price.id))
        }},
        { upsert: true }
      )
      break
    case "invoice.payment_failed":
      // dunning workflow: notify, retry, eventually deactivate
      break
  }
}

// Fast access check (no Stripe call)
async function hasFeature(userId, feature) {
  const sub = await db.subscribers.findOne({ user_id: userId, status: { $in: ["active", "trialing"] } })
  return sub?.features_cache.includes(feature) ?? false
}

// Indexes
db.subscribers.createIndex({ user_id: 1 })
db.subscribers.createIndex({ stripe_subscription_id: 1 }, { unique: true })
db.invoices.createIndex({ subscriber_id: 1, created_at: -1 })

Trade-offs:

DecisionWhyAlternative
Stripe holds canonical statePCI compliance, dunning, tax, proration doneDIY billing — legal and engineering quagmire
Local copy synced via webhooksFast access checks; no API call per requestLive Stripe API call — latency, rate limits
Cached features_cacheO(1) feature gating readsLive plan lookup — extra read
Webhook-driven updatesAlways reflects payment provider truthPolling — lag, missed events
Plan IDs linked, not embeddedPlan tweaks (price change) are centralEmbedded plan — mass updates needed

Production polish: billing platform — Stripe Billing (best general-purpose), Chargebee/Recurly/Paddle (Paddle is a merchant-of-record for tax simplicity), Maxio/Orb/Metronome/Lago for usage-based billing; tax via Stripe Tax/Avalara/TaxJar/Quaderno; fraud and chargeback handling via Stripe Radar; dunning automated by Stripe (smart retries) or specialized like Baremetrics Recover/Churnkey; payment methods: cards, ACH, SEPA, Apple/Google Pay; self-serve cancellation with retention offers via ProsperStack/Churnkey; analytics: MRR, churn, CAC, LTV via ChartMogul/Baremetrics/ProfitWell; customer portal via Stripe Customer Portal for self-serve plan changes/invoices; webhook reliability: idempotency keys on the consumer, replay UI in Stripe Dashboard; change streams on subscribers trigger feature flag updates via LaunchDarkly/Statsig; audit log all subscription state changes for compliance and support; failed payment notifications to users via Customer.io/Postmark; finance reporting: revenue recognition (ASC 606) handled in Stripe Sigma/Stripe Revenue Recognition.

Question 72

You need to design a database for a learning management system with courses, students, and instructors. How would you structure the collections?

Situation: a learning management system (LMS) with courses, students, and instructors. Courses contain modules, lessons, quizzes, assignments. Students enroll, progress through content, submit assignments, and earn certificates. Instructors author and grade. Reads are heavy (lesson pages); writes are bursty around assignment deadlines.

Approach: five collections. users with role flags (student/instructor); courses hold structure (modules > lessons) embedded for read speed; enrollments link student to course with progress; submissions hold assignment uploads; quiz_attempts hold per-attempt answers and grades. Per-user progress denormalized for fast dashboards.

db.users.insertOne({
  _id: ObjectId(),
  email: "alice@example.com",
  display_name: "Alice",
  roles: ["student"],
  bio: "..."

db.enrollments.updateOne(

    $set: { "progress.current_lesson": nextLessonId,
